Compressive Pile Load Test 
Test Pile P-85 
FY19 MCON P-169 
Water Transmission Line 
Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam, Oahu, Hawaii 
Dear Mr. Ching: 
In accordance with the project design requirements, a static compressive pile load 
test was conducted on a driven test pile (Test Pile No. 85) on May 22 and 23, 2020. This 
letter report presents the results of our field observations, test data, engineering analysis, 
conclusions, and recommendations. 
The static pile load test was conducted on a 16.5-inch octagonal precast, 
prestressed concrete pile. Based on the project specifications, Test Pile P-85 was cast 
with a length of 63 feet and instrumented with 12 vibrating wire embedded strain gages 
(Model No. VCE-4200) manufactured by Geokon. The embedded strain gages were 
installed in pairs at levels spaced at about 10 feet along the load test pile, with the first 
level at about 3 feet above the tip of the pile. The test pile was driven to a depth of about 
54.1 feet below the existing ground surface, which corresponds to a pile tip elevation of 
about -41.1 feet MSL. The approximate location of the load test pile is shown on the Test 
Pile Location Plan, Plate 1.  
At the completion of the initial pile driving, Test Pile P-85 was sticking up 
approximately 9 feet above the existing ground surface, resulting in one level of strain 
gages above the ground surface. To accommodate the compressive pile load test setup 
and testing frame, the top 8 feet of the pile stickup above the ground surface was cutoff, 
resulting in the loss of two strain gages, designated as SG-11 and SG-12. It should be 
noted that as a result of the initial pile driving, two additional strain gages, designated as 
SG-7 and SG-9, malfunctioned and we could receive strain readings from them. Strain 
gage locations within the concrete pile and the final depths below the ground surface after 
pile driving are shown in the following table:

Test Pile P-85 was driven on May 14, 2020. The test pile was driven using a 
Delmag D30-32 hammer delivering a maximum rated energy of 75,438 foot-pounds.  
During the test pile driving, a Geotechnical Quality Control Specialist maintained a record 
of the blow counts and field observations of the driving behavior. The test pile driving log is 
presented as Plate 2. 
Test Pile P-85 was driven to an elevation of about -41.1 feet Mean Sea Level 
(MSL). The test pile was driven to a depth where approximately 9 feet of the pile was left 
above the ground surface. The top 8 feet of concrete was chipped off in order to provide 
sufficient space to fit the load testing frame. Therefore, the total length of the load test pile 
was 54.1 feet measured from the top to the tip of the test pile. A multiplexer was used to 
connect the ten embedded strain gages to a Geokon Micro-10 datalogger, which recorded 
the strains in the embedment strain gages during the compressive pile load test.  
The test pile was loaded in general accordance with ASTM D1143/1143M 
Procedure B – Maintained test procedure. Test Pile P-85 was gradually loaded to a 
maximum test load of 484.5 kips in increment of 42.5 kips. Each load increment was held 
at least 15 minutes or until the rate of movement was less than 0.01 inch per hour. The 
maximum test load was maintained for at least 12 hours while the rate of movement was 
less than 0.01 inch per hour; otherwise, it should be held for 24 hours. 
Subsequently, the test load was unloaded in four decrements. Each unload 
decrement was held for about an hour. The final rebound reading was taken three hours 
after the test load had been removed. Two dial gauges supported on two reference beams 
with mirrors and scales installed on opposite sides of the test pile were used to measure 
pile head displacement. The reference beams were also independently checked for 
potential movement during the test by scales and level surveying. The load test readings 
and the load-displacement curve are presented on Plates 3 and 4, respectively. The 
compressive pile load test results are summarized as follows.

Based on the shape of the curve of the compressive load test and the Davisson 
failure criteria, the 16.5-inch octagonal concrete pile did not fail at the maximum 
compressive test load of about 484.5 kips. The strain changes in the ten embedded strain 
gages were recorded using a Micro-10 datalogger during the compressive pile load test. 
The printouts of the strain gage readings are presented in Appendix A.  
To mitigate the concern of the ground settlement affecting the static load test 
system, an independent measurement system was utilized in addition to the dial gages 
with mirror readings. Settlement measurement of the test pile during loading was 
measured from the reference beams. The reference beams were also measured for 
vertical movement, using the independent engineering level, during the load testing. The 
measurement did not indicate ground settlement during the load testing. Based on the 
results of the measurements and loading curves, we believe the non-conforming items did 
not result in adverse effects of the load test results.  
General information pertaining to the embedment strain gages, calibration sheet for 
the strain gages, and calibration sheet for the load cell are included in Appendix B.
